Jamison Brereton

43 (663)
Agni
Vir┼лpa ─Ас╣Еgirasa
33 verses: g─Бyatr─л, most likely arranged in trcas ╠е
Though it is likely that this hymn is constructed of tr╠еcas, there is little overt unity within the tr╠еcas. On the surface the hymn is a pleasant but generally unremarkable praise of Agni. His ritual functions are showcased throughout, and toward the end the тАЬweтАЭ of the poet and his fellow sacrificers invoke him more and more insistently1114 VIII.43
in this role. But earlier in the hymn there is some nice naturalistic description of fire and fires (vss. 3тАУ10). In verses 14 and 16 the poet emphasizes the kinship between himself and Agni as poet.
Another thematic strain evident in the hymn and asserting itself more and more toward the end is the role of Agni as a unifying focus of various clans and settle ments in the larger ─Аrya community. In several early verses multiple fires are kin dled at once (vss. 4тАУ5). In light of later parts of the hymn, these can be interpreted as the separate family or clan fires, which are later joined conceptually in the single fire to which all the separate groups give allegiance (see esp. vs. 18, also 27, 29). This single fire, found in multiple places but shared by all the clans, is invoked for help in combat in verse 21. AgniтАЩs competitive (vss. 20, 25), martial (vss. 21, 23, 26, 32), and ruling (vs. 24) aspects become more prominent in the second half of the hymn; the sacrificers clearly wish to harness these powers for the good of the whole com munity. Though not insistent, this theme is pervasive and provides a subtle unity to this superficially rambling thirty-three-verse composition.

Jamison Brereton Notes

Agni

Wilson

English translation:

тАЬThese repeaters of laudations recite the praises of the wise creative Agni, the uninterrupted sacrificeс╣ЫтАЭ

Commentary by S─Бyaс╣Зa: с╣Ъgveda-bh─Бс╣гya

Uninterrupted: astс╣Ыta yajvan = the invincible sacrificer

Jamison Brereton

For the inspired poet, the ritual adept, the indestructible sacrificer, for AgniтАФ
these hymns, these praises arise right here.

Jamison Brereton Notes

With Oldenberg I take ├бstс╣Ыta-yajvan- as a karmadh─Бraya, not the bahuvr─лhi of Geldner and Renou, who seem to ignore the evidence of the accent (on which see AiG II.1.80).

Griffith

THESE songs of mine go forth as lauds of Agni, the disposing Sage,
Whose worshipper is ne’er o’erthrawn.

Geldner

Diese Lobesreden und Preislieder auf den redekundigen Meister Agni heben jetzt an, dessen Verehrer nicht zu Fall gebracht wird.

Grassmann

Es regen diese Lieder sich zum Lob des weisen F├╢rderers, Agni’s, des besten Opferers.

Wilson

English translation:

тАЬYour fierce flames, Agni, consume the forest, as wild animals destroy (the plural nts) with their teeth.тАЭ

Commentary by S─Бyaс╣Зa: с╣Ъgveda-bh─Бс╣гya

Wildanimals: arok─Бс╕е = arocam─Бn─Бс╕е pa┼Ыavaс╕е; cf. ┼Ъatapatha Br─Бhmaс╣Зa 3.1.2.18: madhye chidr─Бс╣Зi; (yourfierce flames) glancing, as it were, through the trees

Jamison Brereton

Like brilliants, certainly, are your sharp scintillations, Agni.
With their teeth they snap at the woods.

Jamison Brereton Notes

Geldner takes ─Бrok─Б╠Бс╕е (only here in RV) as тАЬMaschenтАЭ (mesh), and this does seem to be the meaning in late Vedic. This idiomatic sense presumably developed from тАШlight flashing through openingsтАЩ to the тАШopeningsтАЩ themselves. However, mesh or netting does not seem a particularly apt comparison here, and I prefer to take the word in a more literal, but still concrete, sense, esp. since rocate appears several times in the hymn (8c, 10b). By тАШbrilliantsтАЩ I mean gems or gem-like objects (rhinestones, e.g., had they been invented then) that catch and flash light. A more abstract sense, like тАШflashesтАЩ or тАШflaresтАЩ, risks near identity with what itтАЩs being compared with (tv├нс╣гaс╕е).

The force of the particle pile-up gh├йd ├бha is not entirely clear to me, but this poet is partial to it. See gh├йd тАж ├бh─Б in 30, as well as gh├йd in 29, ├бha in 8. I have not found gh├йd (тАж) ├бha elsewhere in the RV.

Griffith

Thy sharpened flames, O Agni, like the gleams of light that glitter through,
Devour the forests with their teeth.

Geldner

Deine scharfen Gluten, Agni, sind ganz wie durchsichtige Maschen; mit den Z├дhnen schnappen sie nach den H├╢lzern.

Grassmann

So recht wie lichter Funken Schein ist, Agni, dein Ergl├дnzen hell, Mit Z├дhnen kaut die H├╢lzer er.

Elizarenkova

Jamison Brereton Notes

vс╣Ы╠Бthak is found only in these two vss. It is generally considered to be a formal cross of vс╣Ы╠Бth─Б тАШat willтАЩ with pс╣Ы╠Бthak тАШseparatelyтАЩ (see EWA s.v., AiG III.231, Renou ad loc.), a form of which appears in repeated p─Бdas later in the hymn (18b=29b), and to maintain the semantics of the former (Geldner тАШj├дhтАЩ [тАШprecipitouslyтАЩ – a rather extended sense], Renou тАШ├а leur gr├йтАЩ). S─Бyaс╣Зa, however, simply glosses it as pс╣Ыthak. I am reluctantly sympathetic to S─Бyaс╣ЗaтАЩs opinion, as тАШat willтАЩ does not fit the contexts well, esp. 5a. (Both Geldner and Renou tr. it with p─Бda b in 4, not in its proper place.) X.91.7 ─Б╠Бte yatante rathy├▓ y├бth─Б pс╣Ы╠Бthak, adduced by Geldner, echoes our 4c. The published translation reflects the S─Бyaс╣Зa gloss. However, on returning to this passage, I find the S─Бyaс╣Зa solution too convenient and entirely unmotivated, but still remain unsatisfied with the connection with vс╣Ы╠Бth─Б and its suggested crossing with pс╣Ы╠Бthak. That the formation of both vс╣Ы╠Бth─Б and prthak ╠е╠Б is murky does not help. I do not have anything resembling a solution, but IтАЩm inclined to think that v├н тАШapartтАЩ is somehow implicated. Perhaps via an (unfortunately unattested) -a├▒c-stem, *vi ya├▒c- тАШfacing separate directionsтАЩ, whose neut. adv. *vi yak could have been assimilated to pс╣Ы╠Бthak given their similiarity of meaning. Cf. the similarly formed v├нс╣гva├▒c- тАШfacing in separate directionsтАЩ, whose neut. appears two hymns later in a suggestive collocation, VIII.45.8 тАж v├нс╣гvag y├бth─Б.

Wilson

English translation:

тАЬMaking the plural nts his food, Agni devouring them is never satiated, but falls again upon the young(shrubs).тАЭ

Jamison Brereton

Making the plants his wellspring (of nourishment), snapping (at them), Agni does not become extinguished,
as he comes once again to the tender ones.

Griffith

Making the plants his nourishment, Agni devours and wearies not,
Seeking the tender shrubs again.

Geldner

Die Pflanzen zu seiner Nahrung machend und schnappend kommt Agni nicht zu kurz, der wieder in die jungen Triebe eingeht.

Grassmann

Die Pflanzen w├дhlend sich zur Kost, l├дsst Agni nicht zu kauen ab Und eilt zu immer frischen hin.

Elizarenkova

English translation:

тАЬBowing down (the trees) with his tongues (of flame), and blazing with splendour, Agni shines in theforests.тАЭ

Jamison Brereton

Bending back and forth with his tongues, flickering here and there with his flame,
Agni shines brightly in the woods.

Jamison Brereton Notes

On ja├▒j see comm. ad I.168.7.

Griffith

Bending him down with all his tongues, he flickers with his fiery glow
Splendid is Agni in the woods.

Geldner

Mit seinen Zungen auf und ab fahrend, mit der Flamme hin und her flackernd leuchtet Agni in den W├дldern.

Grassmann

Mit seinen Zungen beugend sich und funkelnd mit der Flamme Glanz Erstrahlet Agni in dem Holz.

Wilson

English translation:

тАЬYour station, Agni, is in the waters; you cling to the plural nts, and becoming their embryo, are born again.тАЭ

Jamison Brereton

In the waters is your seat, Agni. You grow through the plants.
While (still) being in their womb, you are born again.

Jamison Brereton Notes

Assuming with the Pp., Macdonell (VGS ┬з48a), and Lubotsky (s.v. s├б) that sa├║с╣гadh─лс╕е represents s├б(с╕е) ├│с╣гadh─лс╕е, this sandhi contravenes the standard treatment; cf. I.103.5, X.88.10 s├б ├│с╣гadh─лс╕е. The s├б with 2nd ps. reference also does not conform to my rules for this usage, as it is not in an imperatival clause. I do not have an answer, though poetic factors may have had some influence: note the preceding p─Бda (ap)s├║ … s├бdhi(с╣г) тАж, which is a good match for the three syllables in sa├║с╣гadh─л(r).

Griffith

Agni, thine home is in the floods: into the plants thou forcest way,
And as their Child art born anew.

Geldner

Im Wasser ist deine Wohnstatt, Agni. Du w├дchst in den Pflanzen nach, und in ihrem Mutterleib befindlich wirst du wiedergeboren.

Grassmann

In Wassern, Agni, ist dein Sitz und den Gew├дchsen strebst du zu, Dem Mutterleib entspringst du neu.

Elizarenkova

English translation:

тАЬYour lustre, Agni, lambent in the mouth of the ladle, shines when offered from (the oblation of) butter.тАЭ

Jamison Brereton

This flame of yours, Agni, when bepoured, blazes up from the ghee, kissing the offering spoons on the mouth.

Jamison Brereton Notes

I prefer to maintain the older gloss тАШkissтАЩ for niс╣Гs rather than flg. Got┼Н (200-201; cf. EWA s.v., Lubotsky s.v. тИЪnas) in the colorless substitution тАШapproachтАЩ. Even if n├нс╣Гsa- is in origin a redupl. pres. to тИЪnas, passages like this, with m├║khe тАШon the mouthтАЩ, support the richer semantics, which could have developed from an earlier тАШapproachтАЩ, used metaphorically or euphemistically.

Worshipped with offerings shines thy flame, O Agni, from the sacred oil,
With kisses on the ladle’s mouth.

тАЬLet us adore with hymns Agni, the granter (of desires), the eater of the ox, the eater of the marrow, onwhose back the libation is poured.тАЭ

To him whose food is oxen, whose food is barren cows, to the ritual adept with soma on his backтАФ
to Agni we would do honor with praises.

Who bears the Soma on his back.

Who feedeth on bull and cow,
The disposer, backed with Soma.

Wilson

English translation:

тАЬYou, Agni, are kindled by Agni; a sage by a sage, saint by a saint, a friend by a friend.тАЭ

Commentary by S─Бyaс╣Зa: с╣Ъgveda-bh─Бс╣гya

A saint by asaint: San, sat─Б = vidyam─Бnaс╕е, vidyam─Бnena; Aitareya Br─Бhmaс╣Зa 1.16: the fire was produced by frictionfrom the two araс╣Зis and was thrown into the ─Бhavan─лya fire, in the atithyeс╣гс╣нi ceremony; in the verse tvamhyagne…, the one vipra (a sage) means one Agni, the other vipra the other Agni; the one san (being, existing)means the one, the other san (in sat─Б) the other Agni (Haug)

Jamison Brereton

For youтАФo Fire by fire, a poet by a poet, the real (thing) by a
real (man),
a comrade by a comradeтАФare kindled.

Jamison Brereton Notes

agne has to be tr. тАЬFire,тАЭ rather than the usual тАЬAgni,тАЭ because otherwise the verbal play is lost. The constant interplay in the RV between physical fire and the god Agni is hard to render in tr. because of the PN problem.

Griffith

For thou, O Agni, by the fire, Sage by the Sage, Good by the Good,
Friend by the Friend, art lighted up.

Keith

Thou, O Agni, by Agni,
The sage by the sage, the good by the good,
The comrade by the comrade, art kindled.

Geldner

Denn du, Agni, wirst an Agni, der Redekundige an dem Redekundigen, der Treffliche an dem Trefflichen, der Freund an dem Freund entz├╝ndet.

Grassmann

Vom Weisen wirst du Weiser ja, o Glut, von Glut, vom Helden Held, Ein Freund vom Freunde angefacht.

Elizarenkova

English translation:

тАЬMy praises hasten to you, Agni, as cows enter their stalls (to give milk) to the thirsting calves.тАЭ

Jamison Brereton

And you, Agni, have my praises reachedтАФ(the praises generated) for the bellowing one who yearns for (them)тАФ
like cows their cow-stall.

Jamison Brereton Notes

Despite the case disharmony between acc. tv─Б in a and the dat. phrase in b, I take them both as referring to Agni (so also Oldenberg). Geldner takes the dat. in b as part of the simile in c, referring to a calf awaiting the cows coming to its stall. (RenouтАЩs tr.

seems to combine the two.) But vs. 2a ├бsmai te pratih├бryate (and cf. VIII.44.2 pr├бti тАж harya) establishes Agni as the primary referent here, though a secondary connection with a calf (via the bellowing) isnтАЩt impossible. As for the case difference, vs. 2 provides a possible solution, since the verb there is j├бn─Бmi тАШI generateтАЩ, construed with the dat. of benefit. Hence my тАЬ(praises generated)тАЭ here.

Griffith

My praises, Agni, go to thee, as the cows seek the stall to meet,
The lowing calf that longs for milk.

Geldner

Und zu dir, Agni, sind meine Loblieder wie die K├╝he zum br├╝llenden, erwartenden Kalbe in den Stall gekommen.

Grassmann

Dir eilen meine Lieder zu, wie K├╝he, Agni, in den Stall Zum Kalbe, das verlangend br├╝llt.

Elizarenkova

You, Agni, prizewinner on the drives, do those who stretch out their ceremony
reverently invoke as draft-horse (of the sacrifice), as Hotar.

’nose who spin out the sacrifice.

тАЬYou are the lord, you behold all people alike in many plural ces; we therefore invoke you in battles.тАЭ

Jamison Brereton

Because you are of the same aspect in many places, preeminent
throughout all the clans,
in combats we call upon you.

Griffith

In many a place, the same in look art thou, a Prince o’er all the tribes
In battles we invoke thine aid.

Wilson

English translation:

тАЬWe worship with praises you, Agni, who are born in heaven or in the waters, elicited by strength.тАЭ

Commentary by S─Бyaс╣Зa: с╣Ъgveda-bh─Бс╣гya

Bornin heaven: as the sun in heaven, as lightning in the waters, (i.e., in the firmament) and as genitive rated on earth byfriction

Jamison Brereton

O might-made Agni, whether you are born in heaven or born in the waters,
we call upon you with hymns.

Griffith

O Agni, made by strength! be thou born in the heavens or born in floods,
As such we call on thee with songs.

Geldner

Ob du, Agni, im Himmel geboren oder im Wasser geboren bist, du Krafterzeugter, wir rufen dich mit Lobesworten an.

Grassmann

Ob, Agni, kraftgeborner, du vom Himmel stammst, ob aus der Flut, So rufen wir mit Liedern dich.

Elizarenkova

English translation:

тАЬAll these people, the inhabitants (of the earth), offer severally to you (sacrificial) food for your eatingand enjoyment.тАЭ

Jamison Brereton

To you do these peoples here, all the lovely settlements separately, impel the wellspring (of nourishment) to be eaten.

Griffith

Yea, all the people, all the folk who have good dwellings, each apart,
Send food for thee to eat thereof.

Geldner

Grassmann

Dir senden diese Menschen hier, die angesessnen weit und breit, Die Nahrung zum Geniessen zu.

Elizarenkova

тАЬShining forth, Agni, like the rising sun, displaying your strength by your beams, you destroy thedarkness.тАЭ

You, Agni, with far-radiant goods, dispatching (darkness) like the sun with its rays,
vaunting yourself, you keep smashing the dark shades.

So thou, O Agni rich in light, beaming like Surya with thy rays
Boldly demolishest the gloom,
